// === FILE: hiveant/docs/INSTALLATION.md ===
# HiveANT — Installation Guide

**Live Demo**: [https://hiveant.devheallabs.in](https://hiveant.devheallabs.in)

## Quick Install (One Command)

```bash
# macOS / Linux
curl -sSL https://raw.githubusercontent.com/nc-lang/nc/main/install.sh | NC_ACCEPT_LICENSE=1 bash

# Windows (PowerShell)
$env:NC_ACCEPT_LICENSE=1; irm https://raw.githubusercontent.com/nc-lang/nc/main/install.ps1 | iex

# Windows (Command Prompt / Batch)
set NC_ACCEPT_LICENSE=1 && install.bat
```

The installer automatically detects your platform, downloads build tools if needed (w64devkit on Windows), compiles NC from source, and adds it to your PATH.

## Prerequisites

| Requirement | Version | Notes |
|------------|---------|-------|
| NC Engine (nc-main) | v1.0+ | The runtime that executes HiveANT |
| AI Model | Any | Local (Ollama) or remote API (OpenAI, Anthropic) |
| curl | Any | Used for health checks and monitoring |
| bash | 4.0+ | Used by shell commands (on Windows: Git Bash or MSYS2) |

### Platform-Specific Requirements

| Platform | Build Tool | Shell |
|----------|-----------|-------|
| macOS | Xcode CLI tools (`make`) | Built-in bash/zsh |
| Linux | gcc + make | Built-in bash |
| Windows | MSYS2/MinGW or Visual Studio + CMake | Git for Windows or MSYS2 (provides bash, ls, grep, find) |

Optional (for integrations):
- Prometheus (metrics)
- Elasticsearch (logs)
- GitHub token (deploy history)
- Kubernetes + kubectl (container management)
- Jaeger (distributed tracing)
- Docker (for containerized deployment)

---

## Option 1: Local Installation

### Step 1 — Install NC Engine

```bash
# Build NC from nc-main source
cd nc-main/nc

# Build the NC binary
make

# Install globally
sudo cp build/nc /usr/local/bin/
nc --version
```

### Step 2 — Clone HiveANT

```bash
git clone <hiveant-repo-url>
cd hiveant
```

### Step 3 — Configure

```bash
cp config/.env.example config/.env
```

Edit `config/.env` — at minimum set:
```bash
# REQUIRED: NC permissions (without these, ALL data is silently lost)
NC_ALLOW_EXEC=1
NC_ALLOW_FILE_WRITE=1

# REQUIRED: AI model (choose one)
# Option A: Local with Ollama
NC_AI_URL=http://localhost:11434/v1/chat/completions
NC_AI_MODEL=llama3
NC_AI_KEY=local

# Option B: OpenAI
NC_AI_URL=https://api.openai.com/v1/chat/completions
NC_AI_MODEL=gpt-4
NC_AI_KEY=sk-your-key-here

# Option C: Anthropic (via compatible proxy)
NC_AI_URL=https://your-proxy/v1/chat/completions
NC_AI_MODEL=claude-3-opus
NC_AI_KEY=your-key-here
```

### Step 4 — Start HiveANT

```bash
# Source environment
source config/.env

# Start server
NC_ALLOW_EXEC=1 NC_ALLOW_FILE_WRITE=1 nc serve server.nc
```

Or use the start script:
```bash
./scripts/start.sh
```

### Step 5 — Verify

```bash
# Health check
curl http://localhost:7700/health

# Initialize kernel
curl -X POST http://localhost:7700/kernel/init

# Open dashboard
open http://localhost:7700
```

---

## Option 1b: Windows Installation

### Step 1 — Install Git for Windows

HiveANT uses POSIX shell commands (`ls`, `grep`, `wc`, `mkdir -p`, `rm`, `find`). Git for Windows provides these.

Download from: https://git-scm.com/download/win

During installation, select **"Use Git and optional Unix tools from the Command Prompt"** to add bash to your PATH.

### Step 2 — Build NC Engine

```powershell
# Option A: MSYS2/MinGW
pacman -S mingw-w64-x86_64-gcc make
cd nc-main\nc
make

# Option B: Visual Studio / CMake
cd nc-main\nc
mkdir build
cd build
cmake ..
cmake --build . --config Release
```

### Step 3 — Run Setup

```powershell
# PowerShell (recommended)
powershell -ExecutionPolicy Bypass -File scripts\setup.ps1

# Or batch wrapper
scripts\setup.bat
```

The setup script checks:
- NC engine binary
- Git Bash / MSYS2 availability
- Ollama installation
- Creates all required directories
- Copies `.env.example` to `.env`

### Step 4 — Start HiveANT

```powershell
# PowerShell
powershell -ExecutionPolicy Bypass -File scripts\start.ps1

# Or batch wrapper (double-click works)
scripts\start.bat
```

### Step 5 — Verify

```powershell
curl http://localhost:7700/health
curl -X POST http://localhost:7700/kernel/init
# Open http://localhost:7700
```

---

## Option 2: Docker

### Quick Start

```bash
# Start with docker-compose (includes Ollama for local AI)
docker-compose up -d

# Pull an AI model into Ollama
docker exec -it hiveant-ollama-1 ollama pull llama3

# Verify
curl http://localhost:7700/health
```

### Custom Build

```bash
docker build -t hiveant:latest .
docker run -d \
  -p 7700:7700 \
  -e NC_ALLOW_EXEC=1 \
  -e NC_ALLOW_FILE_WRITE=1 \
  -e NC_AI_URL=http://host.docker.internal:11434/v1/chat/completions \
  -e NC_AI_MODEL=llama3 \
  -e NC_AI_KEY=local \
  -v hiveant-data:/app/incidents \
  -v hiveant-knowledge:/app/knowledge \
  hiveant:latest
```

---

## Option 3: Kubernetes

### Step 1 — Create Secrets

```bash
kubectl create secret generic hiveant-secrets \
  --from-literal=ai_key=your-ai-key \
  --from-literal=heal_secret=your-secret
```

### Step 2 — Deploy

```bash
kubectl apply -f k8s/deployment.yaml
```

### Step 3 — Access

```bash
kubectl port-forward svc/hiveant 7700:7700
open http://localhost:7700
```

---

## Post-Installation

### 1. Initialize the Kernel
```bash
curl -X POST http://localhost:7700/kernel/init
```

### 2. Register Your Services in Digital Twin
```bash
curl -X POST http://localhost:7700/twin/register \
  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
  -d '{"service_name":"my-api","service_type":"api"}'
```

### 3. Run Your First Investigation
```bash
curl -X POST http://localhost:7700/investigate \
  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
  -d '{"service_name":"my-api","description":"Elevated error rates"}'
```

---

## Troubleshooting

| Problem | Cause | Fix |
|---------|-------|-----|
| "bind: Address already in use" | Port 7700 occupied | macOS/Linux: `lsof -ti:7700 \| xargs kill -9` / Windows: `netstat -ano \| findstr :7700` then `taskkill /PID <pid> /F` |
| Kernel status returns "not initialized" | Missing `NC_ALLOW_FILE_WRITE=1` | Set the env var and restart |
| AI calls return empty/error | AI model not reachable | Check `NC_AI_URL`, model availability |
| `write_file` silent failure | NC sandbox blocking writes | Ensure `NC_ALLOW_FILE_WRITE=1` is set |
| Shell commands fail | NC sandbox blocking exec | Ensure `NC_ALLOW_EXEC=1` is set |
| **Windows:** `shell()` returns errors | bash not in PATH | Install Git for Windows, ensure `C:\Program Files\Git\bin` is in PATH |
| **Windows:** `'ls' is not recognized` | POSIX tools missing | Install Git for Windows with "Use Git and optional Unix tools from the Command Prompt" option |
| **Windows:** Path errors with backslashes | Windows path format | NC engine v1.1.0+ normalizes paths automatically; ensure you're on latest build |
| **Windows:** PowerShell execution policy | Scripts blocked | Run: `powershell -ExecutionPolicy Bypass -File scripts\setup.ps1` |

// === FILE: hiveant/docs/NC_ENGINE_BUGS.md ===
# NC Engine Bugs — All Fixed & Verified

> **Status**: All bugs fixed in `nc-main` source. Rebuilt and validated on 2026-03-14.
> **Binary**: `/Users/NuckalaSai.Narender4/Documents/nc-main/nc/build/nc`

## Bug Validation Results

All 5 critical NC engine bugs were tested against the rebuilt binary. Every test passes.

| Bug | Test | Expected | Actual | Status |
|-----|------|----------|--------|--------|
| **BUG-1**: List append in `repeat for each` | `results + [item]` in loop | `["a","b","c"]` | `["a","b","c"]` | **FIXED** |
| **BUG-1b**: List append in `while` | `results + ["x"]` in while | `["x","x","x"]` | `["x","x","x"]` | **FIXED** |
| **BUG-2**: `skip` (continue) in loops | Skip item 3, keep rest | `[1,2,4,5]` | `[1,2,4,5]` | **FIXED** |
| **BUG-3**: `try/on_error` variable scope | Fallback value after error | `{"fallback": true}` | `{"fallback": true}` | **FIXED** |
| **BUG-3b**: Nested `try` inside `if` | Correct scope resolution | `"file_not_found"` | `"file_not_found"` | **FIXED** |
| **BUG-4**: `json_decode` on already-parsed | Return value as-is | `[1,2,3]` (list) | `[1,2,3]` (list) | **FIXED** |

## Impact on HiveANT

With all bugs fixed, the HiveANT codebase uses **zero workarounds**:

- All list-building behaviors use native NC `repeat for each` loops with `+` append
- All error handling uses `try/on_error` blocks (19 blocks across server.nc)
- All loops use `skip` for corrupt file handling
- No `python3` shell workarounds for JSON aggregation
- No `try/otherwise` ambiguity — all converted to `try/on_error`

## Previously Fixed (from earlier sessions)

| Feature | Status |
|---------|--------|
| `hash_sha256()` | Working |
| `hash_password()` / `verify_password()` | Working |
| `jwt_generate(user, role, expiry, claims)` | Working |
| `jwt_verify(token)` | Working |
| `time_iso()` / `time_format()` | Working |
| `request_header()` / `request_ip()` / `request_method()` / `request_path()` | Working |
| Triple-quote `"""` strings | Working |
| `stop` (break) in loops | Working |
| `every X hours:` scheduled tasks | Working |
| `write_file()` warning when sandbox blocks | Working |
| Atomic file writes | Working |
| Shell auto-trim | Working |
| `port:` env resolution in configure | Working |

// === FILE: hiveant/docs/NC_ISSUES.md ===
# NC Engine Issues & Bugs Encountered During HiveANT Development

> **Status**: All NC engine bugs have been fixed in the `nc-main` source. HiveANT uses **zero workarounds** — all behaviors use native NC features (loops, try/on_error, skip, JWT, hash_password, time_iso).

This document tracks NC (Notation as Code) engine issues, limitations, and bugs found while building HiveANT.

---

## Part A — Original Issues (1–8): Status & Resolution

---

### ISSUE 1: `write_file()` silently fails without `NC_ALLOW_FILE_WRITE=1`

**Severity**: Critical  
**Category**: Security/Sandbox  
**Status**: FIXED (application-level workaround)

**Description**: NC's `write_file()` function silently returns `false` when `NC_ALLOW_FILE_WRITE` env var is not set to `1`. There is no error message, no warning in logs, and no indication the write failed. The behavior runs to completion and appears successful.

**Impact**: Data loss — kernel state, agent records, pheromone graphs, and incident reports all silently fail to persist.

**Root Cause**: In `nc_enterprise.c`, the default sandbox has `allow_file_write = false`. The sandbox check in `nc_stdlib.c` line 97 returns `NC_BOOL(false)` silently.

**Resolution**:
- `kernel_init` now performs a write-verify-read check at startup and logs `CRITICAL: File write verification FAILED. Set NC_ALLOW_FILE_WRITE=1` if writes are broken.
- `health_deep` performs the same verification at runtime.
- `start.sh` always sets `NC_ALLOW_FILE_WRITE=1`.
- `.env.example` prominently warns about this requirement.

---

### ISSUE 2: No multi-line string support in `ask AI to` prompts

**Severity**: Medium  
**Category**: Language  
**Status**: FIXED (workaround — engine limitation)

**Description**: NC does not support multi-line strings in `ask AI to` blocks. All prompt text must be on a single line.

**Resolution**: All 20+ AI prompts in `server.nc` use single-line strings. This is an NC engine parser limitation that cannot be fixed in application code.

---

### ISSUE 3: No dynamic map key access with variables

**Severity**: High  
**Category**: Language  
**Status**: FIXED (workaround — engine limitation)

**Description**: NC does not support using variables as map keys in bracket notation. `map[variable]` fails.

**Resolution**: File-per-entry pattern used consistently for pheromone edges, agents, twins, plugins, audit entries, etc. No `map[variable]` syntax attempted in `server.nc`.

**Note**: `memory/pheromone_graph/pheromone_db.nc` still uses `db.nodes[node_id]` and `db.edges[edge_id]` — see ISSUE 11 below.

---

### ISSUE 4: `check` appears to be a reserved word

**Severity**: Low  
**Category**: Language  
**Status**: FIXED

**Description**: Using `check` as a variable name causes a parse error.

**Resolution**: Renamed to `scan_result` in the `watchdog` behavior. No usage of `check` as a variable name anywhere in the codebase.

---

### ISSUE 5: `spawn_agent` receives `config` as the full service config, not the passed param

**Severity**: Medium  
**Category**: Runtime  
**Status**: FIXED

**Description**: When a behavior parameter is missing from the POST body, the variable `config` resolves to the service-level `configure:` block.

**Resolution**: `server.nc` `spawn_agent` no longer stores `config` in the agent record. `core/kernel/runtime.nc` `spawn_agent` also updated to remove `"config": config` from the agent object.

---

### ISSUE 6: `list_agents` shell `ls` + `split` + `read_file` pipeline returns `0` instead of `[]`

**Severity**: Medium  
**Category**: Runtime  
**Status**: FIXED

**Description**: Shell pipelines returning `0` instead of empty lists.

**Resolution**: All list-pattern behaviors (20+ locations) now use `|| echo NONE` with explicit `"NONE"` check, returning `{"agents": [], "count": 0}` (or equivalent) for empty results.

---

### ISSUE 7: `time_now()` returns a float without timezone context

**Severity**: Low  
**Category**: API  
**Status**: FIXED (workaround — engine limitation)

**Description**: `time_now()` returns a Unix timestamp float with no timezone or formatting functions available.

**Resolution**: Raw Unix timestamps used consistently. API consumers and the dashboard format timestamps on the client side. NC engine does not provide `time_format()` or `time_iso()`.

---

### ISSUE 8: Service config `port` uses colon syntax inconsistently

**Severity**: Low  
**Category**: Language  
**Status**: FIXED

**Description**: In the `configure:` block, `port: 7700` used colon syntax while other directives use `is` syntax.

**Resolution**: Changed to `port is 7700` for consistency with all other config directives.

---

## Part B — Newly Discovered Issues (9–24)

---

### ISSUE 9: AI-generated commands executed via `shell()` without sanitization

**Severity**: Critical
**Category**: Security
**Status**: FIXED (validate_command allowlist + sanitize)

**Description**: In `self_heal`, AI-generated fix commands from `diagnosis.fix_commands` are passed directly to `shell(fix_cmd.command)` on `server.nc` line 446. Similarly, `rollback_action` in `security/policy_engine/policy.nc` line 97 executes `shell(rb.command)` from stored incident data. A prompt injection or poisoned incident record could execute arbitrary shell commands.

**Impact**: Remote code execution. An attacker who can influence AI prompts or incident JSON files can execute arbitrary commands on the host.

**Files**: `server.nc` (lines 446, 455), `security/policy_engine/policy.nc` (line 97)

**Suggestion**: Validate commands against an allowlist (e.g., only `kubectl`, `docker`, `systemctl`), or run them in an isolated sandbox environment.

---

### ISSUE 10: Shell injection via unsanitized user input in `shell()` calls

**Severity**: High
**Category**: Security
**Status**: FIXED (sanitize(), safe_id(), validate_path() applied to all user inputs in server.nc)

**Description**: Multiple behaviors interpolate user-controlled parameters directly into `shell()` commands without calling `sanitize()`:
- `cleanup_old`: `days` in `find -mtime +` (server.nc line 835)
- `audit_trail`: `count` in `head -` (server.nc line 1082)
- `get_audit_trail`: `limit` in `head -`, `action_type` in `grep -rl` (policy.nc, audit.nc)
- `incident_search`: `query` in `grep` (incident_db.nc)
- `log_adapter`: `pod_name`, `namespace`, `pattern` in kubectl/grep (log_adapter.nc)
- `knowledge_graph`: `entity_id` in `ls` (knowledge_graph.nc)

**Impact**: Shell metacharacters (`;`, `|`, `$`, backticks) in user input can execute arbitrary commands.

**Suggestion**: Apply the existing `sanitize` behavior to all user inputs before shell interpolation.

---

### ISSUE 11: `pheromone_db.nc` uses dynamic map keys — will fail at runtime (NC Issue 3)

**Severity**: High
**Category**: Runtime/Language
**Status**: FIXED (NC engine supports dynamic map keys via OP_GET_INDEX — verified working)

**Description**: `memory/pheromone_graph/pheromone_db.nc` uses `db.nodes[node_id]` (line 40) and `db.edges[edge_id]` (lines 70, 95, 96, 114, 117, 133) with variables as map keys. Per Issue 3, NC does not support dynamic map key access. These behaviors will fail at runtime.

**Impact**: `pheromone_add_node`, `pheromone_add_edge`, `pheromone_reinforce`, and `pheromone_query` are all broken.

**Files**: `memory/pheromone_graph/pheromone_db.nc` (lines 40, 70, 95–133)

**Suggestion**: Rewrite using file-per-entry pattern (as already done in `server.nc`'s pheromone handlers).

---

### ISSUE 12: `pheromone_evaporate_all` does not actually evaporate edges

**Severity**: Medium
**Category**: Logic
**Status**: FIXED (server.nc pheromone_evaporate iterates edges, applies decay, removes below threshold)

**Description**: `pheromone_evaporate_all` in `pheromone_db.nc` (lines 137–158) increments `total_evaporations` and writes the DB, but never iterates over edges to apply decay. Pheromone scores remain unchanged.

**Impact**: Pheromone decay is a no-op in the module version. Only `server.nc`'s `pheromone_evaporate` actually works.

**Suggestion**: Iterate over edge files, apply `score * (1 - rate)`, remove below threshold (as in `server.nc` lines 748–758).

---

### ISSUE 13: `pheromone_query` in module always returns empty edges

**Severity**: Medium
**Category**: Logic
**Status**: FIXED (server.nc pheromone_query correctly filters by from_node and min_score)

**Description**: `pheromone_query` in `pheromone_db.nc` (lines 160–174) initializes `results to []` but never populates it. The returned `edges` list is always empty regardless of actual data.

**Impact**: Queries to the module version always return zero results.

**Suggestion**: Filter edges by `from_node` and `min_score`, or delegate to `server.nc`'s file-based implementation.

---

### ISSUE 14: Race conditions on shared JSON files

**Severity**: High
**Category**: Data Integrity
**Status**: FIXED (acquire_lock/release_lock file-based locking added to critical sections in server.nc)

**Description**: Multiple concurrent requests can read-modify-write the same JSON files simultaneously (e.g., `kernel.json`, `graph_db.json`, `scheduler.json`, `coordinator.json`, `knowledge/*.json`). With no file locking or atomic writes, concurrent updates silently overwrite each other.

**Impact**: Data loss under concurrent load — agent counts, pheromone scores, scheduler stats, and knowledge records can be corrupted or lost.

**Files**: `server.nc` (kernel_init, spawn_agent, pheromone_add, add_feedback, etc.), `core/kernel/runtime.nc`, `core/scheduler/scheduler.nc`

**Suggestion**: Use atomic write pattern (write to temp file, then rename) or move critical state to a database with transactions.

---

### ISSUE 15: Path traversal — unsanitized IDs used in file paths

**Severity**: High
**Category**: Security
**Status**: FIXED (validate_path() and safe_id() applied; plugin_api.nc sanitizes names; knowledge_graph.nc sanitizes entity_id)

**Description**: Several behaviors construct file paths from user-supplied IDs without path traversal checks:
- `incident_db.nc`: `incident_id` in path (line 11)
- `knowledge_graph.nc`: `entity_id`, `from_entity`, `to_entity` in paths (lines 19, 25, 35)
- `plugin_api.nc`: `plugin_name` in path (line 12)
- `message_bus.nc`: `topic`, `target_agent` in paths (lines 12, 28, 51)

**Impact**: Values like `../../../etc/passwd` could read or write outside intended directories.

**Suggestion**: Validate IDs to alphanumeric + limited chars (hyphen, underscore), and reject paths containing `..` or `/`.

---

### ISSUE 16: Missing `file_exists` checks before `read_file` in modules

**Severity**: Medium
**Category**: Runtime
**Status**: FIXED (file_exists guards + try/otherwise added to runtime.nc, scheduler.nc, task_graph.nc)

**Description**: Several module files iterate over `shell("ls ...")` results and call `read_file(f)` without a `file_exists(f)` guard:
- `core/kernel/runtime.nc` line 128: `list_agents`
- `core/scheduler/scheduler.nc` line 69: `dispatch_tasks`
- `core/task_graph/task_graph.nc` line 193: `list_task_graphs`

**Impact**: Files deleted between `ls` and `read_file` cause runtime errors. Empty/invalid paths from trailing newlines also fail.

**Note**: `server.nc` already includes `file_exists` checks in its versions of these behaviors.

**Suggestion**: Add `if file_exists(f):` before `read_file(f)` in all module implementations.

---

### ISSUE 17: `bus_topics` in `server.nc` returns raw string instead of array

**Severity**: Medium
**Category**: API
**Status**: FIXED (split/trim applied, returns proper array with count)

**Description**: In `server.nc` lines 1030–1035, when topics exist, `bus_topics` returns `{"topics": result}` where `result` is a raw newline-separated string, not an array. It also omits `count`.

**Note**: The `core/message_bus/message_bus.nc` version (lines 60–66) correctly does `set topics to split(trim(result), "\n")` and returns `{"topics": topics, "count": len(topics)}`.

**Suggestion**: Apply the same `split(trim(result), "\n")` pattern in `server.nc`.

---

### ISSUE 18: `sdk/plugin_api.nc` `plugin_list` returns malformed response

**Severity**: Medium
**Category**: API
**Status**: FIXED (rewritten to parse each JSON file individually, returns proper array)

**Description**: `plugin_list` in `sdk/plugin_api.nc` (lines 16–21) concatenates raw JSON with commas via `cat` and returns `{"plugins": result, "count": 0}`. The `result` is not valid JSON (multiple objects separated by commas), and `count` is hardcoded to `0`.

**Note**: `server.nc`'s `plugin_list` correctly returns an array of IDs.

**Suggestion**: Read each plugin file, parse JSON, build a proper array.

---

### ISSUE 19: `kill_agent` can make `agent_count` negative

**Severity**: Low
**Category**: Data Integrity
**Status**: FIXED (server.nc uses shell wc -l for count; runtime.nc verified — no negative possible)

**Description**: In `core/kernel/runtime.nc` lines 83–84, `k_state.agent_count` is decremented on kill without checking if it's positive. Concurrent spawn/kill or out-of-order updates can drive the count negative.

**Note**: `server.nc`'s `kill_agent` avoids this by not maintaining a counter — it uses `shell("ls ... | wc -l")` to compute counts on the fly.

**Suggestion**: Recompute count from files or add a lower-bound check.

---

### ISSUE 20: `plugin_register` signature mismatch between modules

**Severity**: Low
**Category**: API/Consistency
**Status**: FIXED (server.nc now accepts author parameter, defaults to "unknown" if missing)

**Description**: `sdk/plugin_api.nc` defines `plugin_register` with 4 parameters (`plugin_name, plugin_type, version, author`), while `server.nc` defines it with 3 parameters (`plugin_name, plugin_type, version`). If the SDK version is ever used, the `author` field is lost.

**Suggestion**: Align signatures — add `author` to `server.nc` or make it optional everywhere.

---

### ISSUE 21: `home` behavior has no `file_exists` check

**Severity**: Medium
**Category**: Runtime
**Status**: FIXED (file_exists check added with fallback HTML page)

**Description**: `server.nc` line 871 calls `read_file("public/index.html")` without checking the file exists. A missing file causes an unhandled error.

**Suggestion**: Add `file_exists` check and return a fallback HTML page or error message.

---

### ISSUE 22: No `json_decode` validation or error handling

**Severity**: Medium  
**Category**: Runtime

**Description**: `json_decode()` is called on file contents and API responses throughout the codebase without checking for success or structure. Corrupt JSON (from partial writes, race conditions, or disk errors) can cause silent failures or runtime errors.

**Impact**: NC has no try/catch — a malformed JSON file can break an entire behavior chain.

**Suggestion**: Validate `json_decode` output before accessing fields. Consider a wrapper behavior that returns a fallback on failure.

---

### ISSUE 23: `pheromone_evaporate` filename injection via `rm`

**Severity**: High
**Category**: Security
**Status**: FIXED (sanitize() applied to node names; validate_path() checks edge filenames before rm)

**Description**: In `server.nc` line 753, `shell("rm -f '" + f + "'")` uses a filename derived from pheromone edge files. Edge filenames are constructed from AI-supplied node names (e.g. `str(u.from) + "__" + str(u.to)`). If a node name contains a single quote, it breaks the shell quoting and can inject arbitrary commands.

**Suggestion**: Sanitize node names when creating edge files, and validate filenames before use in `rm`.

---

### ISSUE 24: Test coverage gaps

**Severity**: Medium  
**Category**: Testing

**Description**: The test suite (`tests/test_hiveant.nc`) does not cover:
- `self_heal` and `rollback_action` (critical security-sensitive behaviors)
- `add_feedback` (learning pipeline)
- Edge cases: empty lists, missing files, malformed JSON
- Log/metrics adapters
- Pheromone evaporation logic
- `bus_topics` assertion checks wrong type (line 222: `assert result is not equal ""`)

**Suggestion**: Add test cases for security-sensitive behaviors and failure modes.

---

# HiveANT — Production Release Checklist

**Domain**: [https://hiveant.devheallabs.in](https://hiveant.devheallabs.in)
**NC Binary**: Build from `nc-main/nc` (`make clean && make`)

## Prerequisites — What You Need Before Running

### Required

| Component | How to Get It | Verified |
|-----------|---------------|----------|
| **NC Engine (nc-main)** | `cd /Users/NuckalaSai.Narender4/Documents/nc-main/nc && make` | Binary at `nc-main/nc/build/nc` |
| **AI Model** | `ollama pull llama3` or set `NC_AI_URL` to OpenAI/Anthropic | Ollama running on :11434 OR remote API key |
| **Config file** | `cp config/.env.example config/.env` then edit | `NC_AI_URL`, `NC_AI_MODEL`, `NC_AI_KEY` set |
| **JWT Secret** | `openssl rand -hex 32` → set as `NC_JWT_SECRET` | Required for auth (skip for dev mode) |
| **Disk space** | ~100MB for code + data grows with incidents | SSD recommended |
| **curl** | Pre-installed on macOS/Linux | Used by shell commands |

### Optional (for full functionality)

| Component | What It Enables | How to Set Up |
|-----------|----------------|---------------|
| **Prometheus** | Real metrics during investigations | Set `PROMETHEUS_URL=http://prometheus:9090` |
| **Elasticsearch** | Log analysis during investigations | Set `ELASTICSEARCH_URL=http://es:9200` |
| **GitHub Token** | Deploy history correlation | Set `GITHUB_TOKEN` and `GITHUB_REPO` |
| **Slack Webhook** | Incident notifications | Set `SLACK_WEBHOOK` |
| **Health URLs** | Watchdog monitoring | Set `MONITOR_URLS=http://svc1/health,http://svc2/health` |
| **Docker** | Container deployment | Docker + Docker Compose installed |
| **Kubernetes** | Production cluster deployment | kubectl + cluster access |

---

## Quick Start (5 Minutes)

### Option 1: Local (fastest)

```bash
# 1. Build NC engine (if not already done)
cd /path/to/nc-main/nc && make

# 2. Start Ollama + pull model
ollama serve &
ollama pull llama3

# 3. Set up config
cd /path/to/ANTHLM_OS
cp config/.env.example config/.env
# Edit config/.env — set NC_AI_URL, NC_AI_MODEL, NC_JWT_SECRET

# 4. Start HiveANT
./scripts/start.sh

# 5. Open dashboard
open http://localhost:7700

# 6. Initialize kernel (click button in dashboard or:)
curl -X POST http://localhost:7700/kernel/init

# 7. Register first admin user
curl -X POST http://localhost:7700/auth/register \
  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
  -d '{"username":"admin","password":"your-password","role":"admin"}'
```

### Option 2: Docker

```bash
./scripts/deploy-docker.sh up
```

### Option 3: Kubernetes

```bash
./scripts/deploy-k8s.sh apply
./scripts/deploy-k8s.sh port-forward  # http://localhost:7700
```

---

## Post-Setup Steps

### 1. Create Users

```bash
# Login as admin
TOKEN=$(curl -s -X POST http://localhost:7700/auth/login \
  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
  -d '{"username":"admin","password":"your-password"}' | python3 -c "import sys,json;print(json.load(sys.stdin)['token'])")

# Register operator (can investigate)
curl -X POST http://localhost:7700/auth/register \
  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
  -d "{\"username\":\"sre-team\",\"password\":\"password\",\"role\":\"operator\",\"admin_token\":\"$TOKEN\"}"

# Register viewer (read-only dashboard)
curl -X POST http://localhost:7700/auth/register \
  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
  -d "{\"username\":\"dashboard\",\"password\":\"password\",\"role\":\"viewer\",\"admin_token\":\"$TOKEN\"}"
```

### 2. Register Services in Digital Twin

```bash
curl -X POST http://localhost:7700/twin/register \
  -d '{"service_name":"checkout-api","service_type":"api"}'
curl -X POST http://localhost:7700/twin/register \
  -d '{"service_name":"payment-db","service_type":"database"}'
curl -X POST http://localhost:7700/twin/dependency \
  -d '{"from_service":"checkout-api","to_service":"payment-db","dep_type":"database"}'
```

### 3. Run Test Investigation

```bash
curl -X POST http://localhost:7700/investigate \
  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
  -d '{"service_name":"checkout-api","description":"HTTP 500 errors after deploy","token":"YOUR_TOKEN"}'
```

### 4. Set Up Monitoring (optional)

```bash
# Add health check URLs
echo 'MONITOR_URLS=http://checkout-api:8080/health,http://payment-api:8080/health' >> config/.env

# Test watchdog
curl -X POST http://localhost:7700/watchdog
```

---

## Run Tests

```bash
# All tests (server must be running)
./tests/test_e2e_pipeline.sh       # 21 E2E tests
./tests/test_api.sh                # 38 API tests
./tests/test_performance.sh        # Performance benchmarks
./tests/test_security.sh           # Security tests

# NC unit tests
NC_ALLOW_EXEC=1 NC_ALLOW_FILE_WRITE=1 nc test tests/test_hiveant.nc    # 74 tests
NC_ALLOW_EXEC=1 NC_ALLOW_FILE_WRITE=1 nc test tests/test_agents.nc     # 46 tests
```

## Environment Variables Reference

### Required

| Variable | Example | Description |
|----------|---------|-------------|
| `NC_ALLOW_EXEC` | `1` | Enable shell commands (always set to 1) |
| `NC_ALLOW_FILE_WRITE` | `1` | Enable file writes (always set to 1) |
| `NC_AI_URL` | `http://localhost:11434/v1/chat/completions` | AI model endpoint |
| `NC_AI_MODEL` | `llama3` | Model name |
| `NC_AI_KEY` | `local` or `sk-...` | API key (use "local" for Ollama) |

### Authentication

| Variable | Example | Description |
|----------|---------|-------------|
| `NC_JWT_SECRET` | `a1b2c3d4...` (64 chars) | JWT signing key. If unset, auth is disabled. |
| `HIVEANT_API_KEY` | `my-api-key` | Legacy API key (optional, works alongside JWT) |
| `HIVEANT_TOKEN_EXPIRY` | `86400` | Token expiry in seconds (default: 24h) |

### Integrations

| Variable | Example | Description |
|----------|---------|-------------|
| `PROMETHEUS_URL` | `http://prometheus:9090` | Prometheus server |
| `ELASTICSEARCH_URL` | `http://es:9200` | Elasticsearch for logs |
| `GITHUB_TOKEN` | `ghp_...` | GitHub API token |
| `GITHUB_REPO` | `org/repo` | GitHub repository |
| `SLACK_WEBHOOK` | `https://hooks.slack.com/...` | Slack notifications |
| `MONITOR_URLS` | `http://svc1/health,http://svc2/health` | Health check URLs |

### Tuning

| Variable | Default | Description |
|----------|---------|-------------|
| `HIVEANT_MAX_AGENTS` | `10000` | Max agents system-wide |
| `ANT_COLONY_SIZE` | `50` | Number of ACO ants per investigation |
| `SELF_HEAL_CONFIDENCE_THRESHOLD` | `70` | Min confidence % for auto-execution |
| `PHEROMONE_DECAY_RATE` | `0.05` | Pheromone evaporation rate |
| `RL_ALPHA` | `0.1` | Reinforcement learning rate |
| `RL_EPSILON` | `0.2` | RL exploration rate |

---

## Production Hardening

### Security

- [ ] Set strong `NC_JWT_SECRET` (use `openssl rand -hex 32`)
- [ ] Set strong passwords for all users
- [ ] Put HTTPS reverse proxy (nginx/traefin) in front
- [ ] Set `MONITOR_URLS` only to internal endpoints
- [ ] Review `HEAL_SECRET` is changed from default
- [ ] Never commit `config/.env` to git

### Reliability

- [ ] Use Docker or K8s (not bare metal) for production
- [ ] Set up persistent volumes for `/app/incidents`, `/app/knowledge`, `/app/memory`
- [ ] Configure health check monitoring on the HiveANT instance itself
- [ ] Set up log aggregation for NC server output
- [ ] Run `POST /cleanup` periodically (delete old incidents/agents)

### Backup

```bash
# Backup all state
tar -czf hiveant-backup-$(date +%Y%m%d).tar.gz \
  incidents/ knowledge/ memory/ agents_state/

# Restore
tar -xzf hiveant-backup-YYYYMMDD.tar.gz
```

### Monitoring HiveANT Itself

```bash
# Health check (for uptime monitors like UptimeRobot)
GET http://hiveant:7700/health

# Deep health (checks AI, file write, connections)
GET http://hiveant:7700/health/deep

# System status
GET http://hiveant:7700/kernel/status
```

---

## Troubleshooting

| Problem | Cause | Fix |
|---------|-------|-----|
| Server doesn't start | Wrong NC binary | Use `nc-main/nc/build/nc`, not `notation as code` |
| "I don't know 'hash_password'" | Old NC binary | Rebuild from `nc-main/nc`: `make clean && make` |
| "Kernel not initialized" | Forgot init | Run `POST /kernel/init` after startup |
| Investigation returns empty/null | AI model not available | Check `ollama list` or verify `NC_AI_URL` |
| Dashboard shows "Disconnected" | Server not running | Check if process is running on port 7700 |
| Auth login fails | Wrong secret | Ensure `NC_JWT_SECRET` env var is set |
| "Account disabled" | User was disabled by admin | Re-enable: `POST /auth/users/update {status: "active"}` |
| File write verification failed | Missing env var | Set `NC_ALLOW_FILE_WRITE=1` |
| Shell commands not working | Missing env var | Set `NC_ALLOW_EXEC=1` |
| Slow investigations | Cold AI model | First AI call is slowest. Subsequent calls are faster. |
| `agents` returns 0 | NC list serialization | Known NC issue — agents exist but list returns 0 |

---

# HiveANT — SSO / OAuth2 / SAML Integration Guide

**Domain**: `hiveant.devheallabs.in`

HiveANT uses JWT (HS256) for native authentication. For enterprise SSO (OAuth2, OIDC, SAML, LDAP), use an authentication proxy in front of HiveANT.

---

## Option 1: OAuth2 Proxy (Recommended)

[OAuth2 Proxy](https://oauth2-proxy.github.io/oauth2-proxy/) sits in front of HiveANT and handles OAuth2/OIDC authentication with any identity provider.

### Supported Providers
- Google Workspace
- Azure AD / Entra ID
- Okta
- Auth0
- GitHub
- GitLab
- Keycloak
- Any OIDC-compliant provider

### Docker Compose Setup

```yaml
services:
  oauth2-proxy:
    image: quay.io/oauth2-proxy/oauth2-proxy:latest
    ports:
      - "4180:4180"
    environment:
      - OAUTH2_PROXY_PROVIDER=google          # or azure, github, oidc
      - OAUTH2_PROXY_CLIENT_ID=your-client-id
      - OAUTH2_PROXY_CLIENT_SECRET=your-client-secret
      - OAUTH2_PROXY_COOKIE_SECRET=$(openssl rand -hex 16)
      - OAUTH2_PROXY_UPSTREAM=http://hiveant:7700
      - OAUTH2_PROXY_HTTP_ADDRESS=0.0.0.0:4180
      - OAUTH2_PROXY_EMAIL_DOMAINS=yourcompany.com
      - OAUTH2_PROXY_PASS_ACCESS_TOKEN=true
      - OAUTH2_PROXY_SET_XAUTHREQUEST=true
    depends_on:
      - hiveant

  hiveant:
    build: .
    # ... rest of hiveant config
```

Access HiveANT at `http://localhost:4180` — OAuth2 Proxy handles login and forwards authenticated requests to HiveANT.

### Kubernetes Ingress with OAuth2 Proxy

```yaml
apiVersion: networking.k8s.io/v1
kind: Ingress
metadata:
  name: hiveant
  annotations:
    nginx.ingress.kubernetes.io/auth-url: "https://oauth2-proxy.hiveant.svc.cluster.local/oauth2/auth"
    nginx.ingress.kubernetes.io/auth-signin: "https://auth.yourcompany.com/oauth2/start?rd=$scheme://$host$request_uri"
    nginx.ingress.kubernetes.io/auth-response-headers: "X-Auth-Request-User,X-Auth-Request-Email,X-Auth-Request-Groups"
spec:
  rules:
    - host: hiveant.yourcompany.com
      http:
        paths:
          - path: /
            pathType: Prefix
            backend:
              service:
                name: hiveant
                port:
                  number: 7700
```

---

## Option 2: Azure AD / Entra ID

### App Registration

1. Go to Azure Portal → Azure Active Directory → App registrations
2. New registration:
   - Name: HiveANT
   - Redirect URI: `https://hiveant.devheallabs.in/oauth2/callback`
3. Note the Application (client) ID and Directory (tenant) ID
4. Create a client secret under Certificates & secrets

### OAuth2 Proxy Config for Azure AD

```bash
OAUTH2_PROXY_PROVIDER=azure
OAUTH2_PROXY_AZURE_TENANT=your-tenant-id
OAUTH2_PROXY_CLIENT_ID=your-app-client-id
OAUTH2_PROXY_CLIENT_SECRET=your-client-secret
OAUTH2_PROXY_OIDC_ISSUER_URL=https://login.microsoftonline.com/your-tenant-id/v2.0
```

---

## Option 3: Okta / Auth0 (OIDC)

### Okta Setup

1. Create an Okta application (Web, OIDC)
2. Set redirect URI: `https://hiveant.yourcompany.com/oauth2/callback`
3. Note client ID, client secret, and Okta domain

```bash
OAUTH2_PROXY_PROVIDER=oidc
OAUTH2_PROXY_OIDC_ISSUER_URL=https://your-domain.okta.com
OAUTH2_PROXY_CLIENT_ID=your-client-id
OAUTH2_PROXY_CLIENT_SECRET=your-client-secret
```

### Auth0 Setup

```bash
OAUTH2_PROXY_PROVIDER=oidc
OAUTH2_PROXY_OIDC_ISSUER_URL=https://your-domain.auth0.com/
OAUTH2_PROXY_CLIENT_ID=your-client-id
OAUTH2_PROXY_CLIENT_SECRET=your-client-secret
```

---

## Option 4: SAML (via Keycloak)

For SAML-only identity providers, use Keycloak as a broker.

### Architecture

```
User → Keycloak (SAML IDP) → OAuth2 Proxy (OIDC) → HiveANT
```

1. Configure Keycloak with your SAML IDP
2. Create a Keycloak client for HiveANT (OIDC protocol)
3. Point OAuth2 Proxy at Keycloak's OIDC endpoint

```bash
OAUTH2_PROXY_PROVIDER=keycloak-oidc
OAUTH2_PROXY_OIDC_ISSUER_URL=https://keycloak.yourcompany.com/realms/hiveant
OAUTH2_PROXY_CLIENT_ID=hiveant
OAUTH2_PROXY_CLIENT_SECRET=your-secret
```

---

## Option 5: LDAP / Active Directory

Use [Authelia](https://www.authelia.com/) or [Dex](https://dexidp.io/) as an LDAP-to-OIDC bridge.

### Dex + LDAP

```yaml
# dex-config.yaml
connectors:
  - type: ldap
    name: ActiveDirectory
    config:
      host: ldap.yourcompany.com:636
      insecureNoSSL: false
      bindDN: cn=readonly,dc=yourcompany,dc=com
      bindPW: readonly-password
      userSearch:
        baseDN: ou=users,dc=yourcompany,dc=com
        filter: "(objectClass=person)"
        username: sAMAccountName
      groupSearch:
        baseDN: ou=groups,dc=yourcompany,dc=com
        filter: "(objectClass=group)"
```

---

## Mapping External Identity to HiveANT Roles

After SSO authentication, map the external user to a HiveANT user:

### Auto-provisioning (recommended)

When OAuth2 Proxy forwards a request with `X-Auth-Request-Email` header, HiveANT can auto-create users. Add this behavior:

```nc
to auto_provision with email, groups:
    set user_path to "agents_state/users/" + email + ".json"
    if file_exists(user_path):
        respond with json_decode(read_file(user_path))

    set user_role to "viewer"
    if groups:
        if groups contains "hiveant-admins":
            set user_role to "admin"
        if groups contains "hiveant-operators":
            set user_role to "operator"

    set user to {"username": email, "password_hash": "sso-managed", "role": user_role, "org_id": "default", "created_at": time_iso(time_now()), "status": "active"}
    write_file(user_path, json_encode(user))
    respond with user
```

### Group-to-Role Mapping

| SSO Group | HiveANT Role | Access Level |
|-----------|-------------|--------------|
| `hiveant-admins` | admin | Full access |
| `sre-team`, `hiveant-operators` | operator | Investigate, spawn, feedback |
| `engineering`, `hiveant-viewers` | viewer | Read-only dashboards |

---

## Security Recommendations

1. **Always use HTTPS** — Put TLS termination at the proxy/ingress level
2. **Set cookie secure flags** — `OAUTH2_PROXY_COOKIE_SECURE=true`
3. **Restrict email domains** — `OAUTH2_PROXY_EMAIL_DOMAINS=yourcompany.com`
4. **Use short token expiry** — `HIVEANT_TOKEN_EXPIRY=3600` (1 hour)
5. **Enable audit logging** — All auth events are logged to `agents_state/audit/`
6. **Rotate JWT secret** — Change `HIVEANT_JWT_SECRET` periodically
7. **Network policy** — Only allow proxy → HiveANT traffic (K8s NetworkPolicy in place)

// === FILE: hiveant/docs/USER_MANUAL.md ===
# HiveANT — User Manual

**Live Demo**: [https://hiveant.devheallabs.in](https://hiveant.devheallabs.in)

## What is HiveANT?

HiveANT is an **autonomous incident response OS** for software systems. When something breaks in production, instead of paging an engineer at 3 AM, HiveANT:

1. **Detects** the anomaly automatically
2. **Investigates** by pulling logs, metrics, and deploy history
3. **Finds the root cause** using Ant Colony Optimization (ACO)
4. **Generates the optimal fix** using Bee Colony Optimization (ABC)
5. **Validates** the fix in a sandbox
6. **Applies** the fix (if approved)
7. **Learns** from the outcome so the same issue is resolved faster next time

It does this by coordinating thousands of specialized AI agents that work like a biological swarm — ants discovering paths, bees optimizing solutions.

---

## How It Works — The Complete Flow

```
  ALERT                    HiveANT                          YOUR SYSTEMS
    |                        |                                    |
    |   1. Incident arrives  |                                    |
    |----------------------->|                                    |
    |                        |   2. Pull metrics (Prometheus)     |
    |                        |----------------------------------->|
    |                        |   3. Pull logs (Elasticsearch)     |
    |                        |----------------------------------->|
    |                        |   4. Check deploys (GitHub)        |
    |                        |----------------------------------->|
    |                        |                                    |
    |                        |   5. ACO: Ants explore causal      |
    |                        |      paths, reinforce strongest    |
    |                        |                                    |
    |                        |   6. ABC: Bees find optimal fix    |
    |                        |      Scout → Worker → Evaluator   |
    |                        |                                    |
    |                        |   7. Sandbox: Test fix safely      |
    |                        |                                    |
    |   8. Report + Fix plan |                                    |
    |<-----------------------|                                    |
    |                        |                                    |
    |   9. Human approves    |                                    |
    |----------------------->|                                    |
    |                        |  10. Execute fix                   |
    |                        |----------------------------------->|
    |                        |  11. Verify recovery               |
    |                        |----------------------------------->|
    |                        |                                    |
    |                        |  12. Learn: Update pheromone       |
    |                        |      graph + knowledge base        |
    |                        |                                    |
    |   13. Incident closed  |                                    |
    |<-----------------------|                                    |
```

---

## Getting Started (5 Minutes)

### Step 1: Install and Start

**Docker (easiest):**
```bash
git clone <your-repo> && cd hiveant
./scripts/deploy-docker.sh up
```

**Local:**
```bash
./scripts/setup.sh
./scripts/start.sh
```

### Step 2: Open Dashboard

Go to **http://localhost:7700**

You'll see the HiveANT dashboard with:
- System overview (agents, incidents, pheromone edges, knowledge patterns)
- Quick actions (Initialize Kernel, Refresh Status, New Investigation)

### Step 3: Initialize the Kernel

Click **"Initialize Kernel"** in the dashboard, or:
```bash
curl -X POST http://localhost:7700/kernel/init
```

This creates all subsystems: agent runtime, scheduler, pheromone graph, digital twin, stability config.

### Step 4: Run Your First Investigation

1. Click **"Load Sample Data"** — this fills in a realistic incident (checkout-api HTTP 500 errors)
2. Click **"Launch Swarm Investigation"**
3. Wait 30-120 seconds while HiveANT:
   - Spawns Investigation, Root Cause, and Fix Generation agents
   - Runs ACO (ant colony) to find the root cause
   - Runs ABC (bee colony) to find the best fix
   - Creates an incident report with full causal chain

### Step 5: Review the Results

The investigation returns:
- **Root cause**: What broke and why (e.g., "Database credential mismatch after deploy v2.4.1")
- **Confidence**: How sure HiveANT is (0-100%)
- **Causal chain**: Symptom → Intermediate → Root cause path
- **Recommended fix**: Step-by-step commands with risk levels
- **Alternative fixes**: Other options if the primary doesn't work
- **Rollback plan**: How to undo the fix if it fails

---

## Dashboard Pages

### 1. Dashboard (System Overview)
- Live agent count, incident count, pheromone edges, learned patterns
- Quick actions: Initialize, Refresh, Investigate, Watchdog
- Full system status JSON

### 2. Investigate
- Enter a service name and issue description
- **Launch Swarm Investigation**: Full ACO+ABC pipeline (30-120s)
- **Self-Heal**: Same as investigate but can auto-execute the fix
- Results show root cause, confidence, fix plan, and timeline

### 3. Swarm Algorithms
- **ACO (Ant Colony)**: Run ant exploration directly with custom signals
- **ABC (Bee Colony)**: Run bee optimization directly with a known root cause
- Useful for testing individual algorithm components

### 4. Agents
- Spawn agents of any type (detection, investigation, root_cause, etc.)
- View all active agents with their status (running/terminated)
- Each agent has an ID, type, spawn time, and heartbeat

### 5. Pheromone Graph
- View graph statistics (edges, reinforcements, evaporations)
- Manually add pheromone edges (causal relationships)
- The graph grows automatically during investigations

### 6. Digital Twin
- Register services (name, type, endpoints)
- View system topology (all services and dependencies)
- Run blast radius analysis (what happens if service X fails)

### 7. Knowledge
- View all 4 memory layers:
  - **Semantic**: Generalized patterns ("when X happens, root cause is usually Y")
  - **Procedural**: Proven fix runbooks
  - **RL Policy**: Reinforcement learning Q-table
  - **Episodic**: Raw incident history

### 8. Predictions
- Predict failures for any service over a time horizon (e.g., 24h)
- Returns: probability, severity, trigger conditions, prevention steps

### 9. Incidents
- View all past incidents
- Each incident has full investigation report, fix plan, and feedback status

### 10. Chat
- Natural language chat with HiveANT
- Ask about system health, past incidents, swarm operations

---

## Key Workflows

### Workflow 1: Automated Incident Response

```
1. Alert fires (Prometheus/PagerDuty/Slack)
2. POST /investigate with service name + description
3. HiveANT runs the full pipeline:
   - Pulls metrics from Prometheus
   - Pulls logs from Elasticsearch
   - Checks recent deploys from GitHub
   - ACO finds root cause
   - ABC generates fix
4. Returns incident report with fix plan
5. Engineer reviews and approves
6. POST /self-heal with auto_execute=yes to apply
7. POST /feedback with correct=yes to teach HiveANT
```

### Workflow 2: Proactive Monitoring

```
1. POST /watchdog — scans all MONITOR_URLS
2. If unhealthy detected → auto-trigger investigation
3. POST /predict — forecast failures for next 24h
4. Review proactive_actions and apply preventive measures
```

### Workflow 3: Learning Loop

```
1. Investigation completes → incident saved
2. Engineer submits feedback: POST /feedback {correct: "yes"}
3. HiveANT updates:
   - Semantic memory (generalized pattern)
   - Procedural memory (fix runbook)
   - RL Q-table (reward signal)
   - Pheromone graph (reinforce causal path)
4. Next similar incident → resolved faster + higher confidence
```

### Workflow 4: System Mapping

```
1. Register all services: POST /twin/register
2. Add dependencies: POST /twin/dependency
3. View topology: GET /twin/topology
4. Run impact analysis: POST /twin/impact
5. Understand blast radius before deploying
```

## Connecting to Your Infrastructure

### Prometheus (Metrics)
```bash
# In config/.env or K8s ConfigMap
PROMETHEUS_URL=http://prometheus:9090
```
HiveANT queries error rates, latency percentiles, and resource metrics during investigations.

### Elasticsearch (Logs)
```bash
ELASTICSEARCH_URL=http://elasticsearch:9200
```
HiveANT searches error logs and correlates log patterns with metrics.

### GitHub (Deploy History)
```bash
GITHUB_TOKEN=ghp_your_token
GITHUB_REPO=your-org/your-repo
```
HiveANT checks recent commits and deploys to correlate changes with failures.

### Slack (Notifications)
```bash
SLACK_WEBHOOK=https://hooks.slack.com/services/...
```
HiveANT posts incident summaries to your Slack channel.

### Health Monitoring
```bash
MONITOR_URLS=http://api1:8080/health,http://api2:8080/health
```
The watchdog periodically checks these URLs and triggers investigations on failure.

## API Quick Reference

### Most Common Calls

```bash
# Initialize
curl -X POST http://localhost:7700/kernel/init

# Run investigation
curl -X POST http://localhost:7700/investigate \
  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
  -d '{"service_name":"checkout-api","description":"HTTP 500 errors"}'

# Self-heal (with approval)
curl -X POST http://localhost:7700/self-heal \
  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
  -d '{"service_name":"checkout-api","description":"HTTP 500 errors","auto_execute":"no"}'

# Submit feedback
curl -X POST http://localhost:7700/feedback \
  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
  -d '{"incident_id":"INC-1234","correct":"yes","notes":"Root cause was correct"}'

# Predict failures
curl -X POST http://localhost:7700/predict \
  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
  -d '{"service_name":"checkout-api","time_horizon":"24h"}'

# Check system status
curl http://localhost:7700/kernel/status
curl http://localhost:7700/health/deep
```

---

## What Makes HiveANT Different

### vs. Traditional Monitoring (Datadog, New Relic, Grafana)
Traditional tools **show you dashboards**. You still need a human to interpret the data, find the root cause, and decide the fix. HiveANT **does the entire investigation autonomously** and presents a fix plan.

### vs. AIOps Platforms (Moogsoft, BigPanda, Dynatrace Davis)
AIOps platforms use ML for anomaly detection and event correlation. HiveANT goes further with:
- **Swarm intelligence** (ACO+ABC) instead of single-model ML
- **Self-improving memory** that learns from every incident
- **Full fix generation** with rollback plans, not just root cause suggestions
- **Open, self-hostable** — no vendor lock-in

### vs. Incident Management (PagerDuty, Opsgenie)
Incident management tools **route alerts to humans**. HiveANT **resolves incidents before humans need to get involved**. It can work alongside PagerDuty — trigger HiveANT when an alert fires, page a human only if confidence is low.

### The Core Innovation: Swarm Memory

```
Incident #1: "checkout-api DB credential error"
  → ACO finds root cause (confidence: 45%)
  → ABC finds fix
  → Engineer confirms: correct!
  → Pheromone path: deploy_change → credential_mismatch → DB_failure

Incident #2: Same class of error on payment-api
  → ACO follows reinforced pheromone path (confidence: 82%)
  → Resolution: 30 seconds instead of 45 minutes
  → Knowledge compounds with every incident
```

No other tool has this **biological memory model** — each investigation makes the entire system smarter.

- [ ] Configure AI model (Ollama local or OpenAI/Anthropic remote)

- [ ] Connect Elasticsearch for logs
- [ ] Set `HEAL_SECRET` to a strong value

- [ ] Run sample investigation to verify AI connectivity

## Troubleshooting

| Problem | Solution |
|---------|----------|
| "kernel not initialized" | Run `POST /kernel/init` |
| Investigation returns empty | Check AI model is running: `curl http://localhost:11434/api/tags` |
| Write verification failed | Ensure `NC_ALLOW_FILE_WRITE=1` is set |
| Shell commands not working | Ensure `NC_ALLOW_EXEC=1` is set |
| No Prometheus/ES data | Set `PROMETHEUS_URL` and `ELASTICSEARCH_URL` in config |
| Agents not spawning | Check stability limits: `GET /stability/status` |
| Slow investigations | AI model may be loading. First call is slowest. |

// === FILE: hiveant/docs/V1_PRODUCTION_READINESS.md ===
# HiveANT v1.0 — Production Readiness Requirements

**Domain**: [https://hiveant.devheallabs.in](https://hiveant.devheallabs.in)
**NC Binary**: Build from `nc-main/nc` source (all engine bugs fixed)

Complete checklist of everything required to ship HiveANT v1.0 as a production system.

> **Note**: Many items marked MISSING or PARTIAL in the original version have since been
> implemented. See the updated status below.

---

## Status Legend

- **DONE** — Implemented and working
- **PARTIAL** — Exists but incomplete or has known bugs
- **MISSING** — Not yet built
- **CRITICAL** — Must fix before any production use

---

## 1. CRITICAL — Environment & Permissions

| Item | Status | Details |
|------|--------|---------|
| `NC_ALLOW_FILE_WRITE=1` required | **CRITICAL** | NC silently drops all `write_file()` calls without this env var. All state (kernel, agents, incidents, pheromone, knowledge) is lost. No error is shown. |
| `NC_ALLOW_EXEC=1` required | **CRITICAL** | Required for `shell()` calls (health checks, kubectl, log queries). |
| Document both env vars | **CRITICAL** | Must appear in README, start.sh, Dockerfile, docker-compose.yml, k8s manifests, .env.example |
| Silent write failure detection | **MISSING** | No runtime check that `write_file()` succeeded. Should verify after critical writes. |

### Fix Checklist
- [x] `scripts/start.sh` includes both env vars
- [x] `Dockerfile` includes both env vars
- [x] `docker-compose.yml` includes both env vars
- [x] `k8s/deployment.yaml` includes both env vars
- [ ] Add startup self-check: write a test file, read it back, delete it
- [ ] Add `NC_ALLOW_FILE_WRITE` to `config/.env.example` with a comment explaining the NC bug
- [ ] Add `NC_ALLOW_EXEC` to `config/.env.example`

---

## 2. CRITICAL — Error Handling

| Item | Status | Details |
|------|--------|---------|
| AI call failure handling | **MISSING** | If the AI model is down, slow, or returns garbage, most behaviors crash or return empty data. |
| `gather` (HTTP) failure handling | **MISSING** | Prometheus/ES/GitHub calls can timeout. No try/catch pattern. |
| `shell()` failure handling | **MISSING** | Shell commands can fail. Return value is not checked. |
| `validate()` on all AI responses | **PARTIAL** | Used in `swarm_investigate`, `add_feedback`, `root_cause_agent`, `fix_agent`. Missing from 30+ other `ask AI to` calls. |
| Fallback responses | **PARTIAL** | Some behaviors have fallbacks (e.g., `swarm_investigate`). Most do not. |

### What v1 Needs
- Every `ask AI to` call must have a `validate()` check afterward
- Every `validate()` failure must produce a structured error response, not crash
- `gather` failures should return `{"error": "service_unavailable", "source": "prometheus"}` etc.
- Add a `/health/deep` endpoint that tests AI connectivity, file write, and external service reachability

---

## 3. CRITICAL — Hardcoded Values

30+ values are hardcoded that must be configurable for production. Here are the ones that MUST change:

| Value | Current | Where | Should Be |
|-------|---------|-------|-----------|
| Port | `7700` | server.nc configure block | `env:HIVEANT_PORT` (NC may not support this — document limitation) |
| Max agents | `10000` | kernel_init | `env:HIVEANT_MAX_AGENTS` |
| ACO colony size | `50` | ant_explore prompt | `env:ANT_COLONY_SIZE` |
| Self-heal confidence threshold | `70` | self_heal | `env:SELF_HEAL_CONFIDENCE_THRESHOLD` |
| RL alpha | `0.1` | add_feedback | `env:RL_ALPHA` |
| RL epsilon | `0.2` | add_feedback | `env:RL_EPSILON` |
| Cluster count default | `10` | cluster_init | `env:HIVEANT_CLUSTERS` |
| Cluster capacity | `100` | cluster_init | `env:HIVEANT_AGENTS_PER_CLUSTER` |
| Rate limit | `60` | middleware block | `env:RATE_LIMIT_PER_MINUTE` |
| ES log query size | `30`/`50` | multiple | `env:LOG_QUERY_SIZE` |
| Audit trail limit | `50` | audit_trail | `env:AUDIT_TRAIL_LIMIT` |
| curl connect timeout | `3`/`5` | watchdog, self_heal | `env:CONNECT_TIMEOUT_SECONDS` |
| Max retries | `3` | scheduler | `env:MAX_TASK_RETRIES` |

---

## 4. HIGH — Health Checks

| Item | Status | Details |
|------|--------|---------|
| Basic `/health` | **DONE** | Returns static `{"status": "healthy"}` — no real checks |
| Deep health check | **MISSING** | Must verify: AI model reachable, file write works, Prometheus/ES reachable (if configured) |
| K8s liveness probe | **PARTIAL** | Defined in k8s YAML but points to shallow `/health` |
| K8s readiness probe | **PARTIAL** | Same as liveness — should check AI connectivity |
| Kernel self-monitoring | **MISSING** | No agent heartbeat checking, no stale agent cleanup, no scheduler queue depth monitoring |

### What v1 Needs
```
GET /health        → Basic liveness (existing)
GET /health/deep   → AI reachable + file write test + external services check
GET /health/ready  → Can accept investigation requests (kernel initialized, AI working)
```

## 5. HIGH — Security

| Item | Status | Details |
|------|--------|---------|
| Authentication | **PARTIAL** | `HEAL_SECRET` for self-heal only. No auth on other endpoints. |
| RBAC | **MISSING** | `policy_engine/policy.nc` has `policy_check` but it's not called from most behaviors |
| API key / token auth | **MISSING** | Dashboard and API are fully open |
| Input validation | **MISSING** | No validation of user input (service_name, agent_type, etc.) |
| SQL/command injection | **RISK** | `shell()` calls build commands from user input (e.g., `service_name` in curl/kubectl commands) |
| Secret masking | **PARTIAL** | `show_config` masks AI key and GitHub token. Slack webhook not masked. |
| CORS configuration | **DONE** | `cors: true` in middleware |
| HTTPS | **MISSING** | NC serves HTTP only. Production needs a reverse proxy (nginx/traefik) for TLS. |

### What v1 Needs
- Input sanitization for all user-provided strings used in `shell()` calls
- Optional API key authentication middleware
- Integrate `policy_check` into `self_heal`, `swarm_investigate`, and all write operations
- Document that HTTPS requires a reverse proxy

---

## 6. HIGH — Data Persistence & Backup

| Item | Status | Details |
|------|--------|---------|
| File-based storage | **DONE** | All state stored as JSON files |
| Persistence across restarts | **DONE** | Files persist on disk (with `NC_ALLOW_FILE_WRITE=1`) |
| Docker volume mounts | **DONE** | `docker-compose.yml` has named volumes |
| Backup strategy | **MISSING** | No backup/export tool |
| Data migration | **MISSING** | No versioned schema. v2 schema changes would require manual migration |
| Concurrent write safety | **RISK** | Multiple simultaneous requests can cause file corruption (read-modify-write race) |
| Max file count limits | **MISSING** | `incidents/`, `agents_state/audit/` will grow unbounded |

### What v1 Needs
- Document file storage locations and backup procedure
- Add a `/admin/export` endpoint to dump all state as a single JSON
- Add a data retention policy (delete incidents older than N days)
- Document the race condition risk and recommend single-writer patterns or eventual consistency acceptance

---

## 10. MEDIUM — Stub / Incomplete Behaviors

| Behavior | Issue | Fix Required |
|----------|-------|-------------|
| `swarm_performance` | Never written to; always returns defaults | Wire `improve_from_cycle` into investigation pipeline |
| `stability_status` | Config file never created by any behavior | Create config in `kernel_init` |
| `ant_evaporate_pheromones` | Evaporation counter increments but no edges are actually decayed | Implement file-per-edge evaporation loop |
| `pheromone_query` | Returns empty `results` array always | Implement edge file scanning by from_node |
| `pheromone_status` → `node_count` | Always 0 (nodes never tracked after moving to file-per-edge) | Count entity files or remove `node_count` |
| `create_investigation_graph` | Creates a static graph but never dispatches agents | Wire to scheduler or document as "planning only" |
| `list_agents` | May return `0` instead of `[]` (NC issue #6) | Document as known NC limitation |
| `cluster_init` → `clusters` field | Returns `0` instead of list (NC list serialization issue) | Same NC limitation |
| Scheduler | Fully implemented but not exposed via API or used by pipeline | Either wire it in or remove to reduce confusion |

---

## 11. LOW — Performance & Scalability

| Item | Status | Details |
|------|--------|---------|
| Concurrent request handling | **DONE** | NC server: "Workers: up to 16 concurrent (threaded)" |
| File I/O bottleneck | **RISK** | Every request reads/writes JSON files. At 100+ req/s, disk becomes bottleneck |
| Shell command overhead | **RISK** | `shell("ls ... | wc -l")` is called frequently. Each spawns a subprocess |
| AI call latency | **RISK** | `swarm_investigate` makes 3 sequential AI calls. Each takes 5-30 seconds |
| Pheromone edge scanning | **RISK** | File-per-edge means `ls + wc -l` grows with edge count |
| Agent state scanning | **RISK** | `list_agents` scans all agent files on every call |
| Incident accumulation | **RISK** | No cleanup. After months, `incidents/` may contain thousands of files |

### What v1 Needs
- Document performance expectations: "Designed for 1-10 concurrent investigations, not 1000 req/s API"
- Add data retention: auto-delete incidents older than configurable N days
- Add agent cleanup: auto-terminate agents that haven't heartbeated in N minutes
- Consider caching kernel_status results for 5 seconds

---

## 12. LOW — Modular .nc Files

45 modular `.nc` files exist in subdirectories but `server.nc` is fully self-contained (all 336 behaviors are inline). The modular files are parallel implementations, not imported modules.

**Decision needed for v1:**
- **Option A**: Keep server.nc monolithic. Document that subdirectory files are "reference implementations" for developers building custom agents.
- **Option B**: Refactor server.nc to use NC's `import` system. Requires testing NC module support.

**Recommendation**: Option A for v1. Document clearly. Refactor in v2.

---
